The memorial is built around a <a href="/wiki/Mast_(sailing)" title="Mast (sailing)">mast</a> salvaged from the <i>Maine</i>’s wreckage. The USS <i>Maine</i> Memorial served as the temporary resting place for foreign heads of state or government, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon" title="Manuel L. Quezon">Manuel L. Quezon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ignacy_Jan_Paderewski" title="Ignacy Jan Paderewski">Ignacy Jan Paderewski</a> of <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, who died in exile in the United States during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">Challenger</a></i> Memorial was dedicated on May 20, 1986, in memory of the crew of flight <a href="/wiki/STS-51-L" title="STS-51-L">STS-51-L</a>, who <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Challenger disaster">died during launch</a> on January 28, 1986. Transcribed on the back of the stone is the text of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Gillespie_Magee,_Jr." title="John Gillespie Magee, Jr.">John Gillespie Magee, Jr.</a> poem <i>High Flight</i>, which was quoted by then President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> when he addressed the disaster. Although many remains were identified and returned to the families for private burial, some were not, and were laid to rest under the marker. Two crew members, <a href="/wiki/Dick_Scobee" title="Dick Scobee">Scobee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Smith_(astronaut)" title="Michael J. Smith (astronaut)">Smith</a>, are buried in Arlington. On February 1, 2004, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> Administrator <a href="/wiki/Sean_O%27Keefe" title="Sean O'Keefe">Sean O'Keefe</a> dedicated a similar memorial to those who died when the Shuttle <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">Columbia</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">broke apart during reentry</a> on February 1, 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA-100">[100]</a></sup> Astronauts <a href="/wiki/Laurel_Clark" title="Laurel Clark">Laurel Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_M._Brown" title="David M. Brown">David Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_P._Anderson" title="Michael P. Anderson">Michael Anderson</a>, who were killed in the Columbia disaster, are also buried in Arlington.</p>
<p>The Lockerbie Cairn is a memorial to the 270 killed in the bombing of <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">Pan Am Flight 103</a> over <a href="/wiki/Lockerbie" title="Lockerbie">Lockerbie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. The memorial is constructed of 270 stones, one for each person killed in the disaster. In section 64, a memorial to the 184 victims of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on the Pentagon was dedicated September 11, 2002. The memorial takes the shape of a pentagon, and lists the names of all the victims that were killed. Unidentified remains from the victims are buried beneath it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pentagon_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pentagon-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 25, 1925, President <a href="/wiki/Calvin_Coolidge" title="Calvin Coolidge">Calvin Coolidge</a> approved a request to erect a Commonwealth <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Sacrifice" title="Cross of Sacrifice">Cross of Sacrifice</a> with the names of all the citizens of the USA who lost their lives fighting in the Canadian forces during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. The monument was dedicated November 11, 1927 and after the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> the names of US citizens who died in those conflicts were added.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Military_Service_for_America_Memorial" title="Women in Military Service for America Memorial">Women in Military Service for America Memorial</a> is adjacent to the Ceremonial Entrance to the cemetery.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Laos_Memorial" title="Laos Memorial">Laos Memorial</a>, or Lao Veterans of America memorial, dedicated to Lao and Hmong veterans who served with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Special_Forces" title="US Special Forces">US Special Forces</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">CIA</a> advisors during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, to defend the Royal <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Laos" title="Kingdom of Laos">Kingdom of Laos</a> from the <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnamese_invasion_of_Laos" title="North Vietnamese invasion of Laos">North Vietnamese invasion of Laos</a> by selling opium to the CIA in exchange for weapons and promises for their own country, is located on Grant Avenue near the eternal flame memorial to U.S. President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, legislation began moving through Congress to approve a "Place of Remembrance" at the cemetery. The memorial will be an <a href="/wiki/Ossuary" title="Ossuary">ossuary</a> designed to contain fragments of remains which are unidentifiable through DNA analysis. The remains will be cremated before placement in the memorial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Burial_procedures">Burial procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Burial procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4776" data-file-width="3576" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg/200px-Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg/300px-Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg/400px-Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arlington_House_Half-mast_28_May_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Arlington House flag flying at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Half-staff" title="Half-staff">half-staff</a>. The flag is lowered during interments.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The flags in the cemetery are flown at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Half-staff" title="Half-staff">half-staff</a> from a half-hour before the first <a href="/wiki/Funeral" title="Funeral">funeral</a> until a half hour after the last funeral each day. Funerals are normally conducted five days a week, excluding weekends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Funerals, including interments and inurnments, average between 27–30 per day. The Cemetery conducts approximately 6,900 burials each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-facts_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-facts-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>With more than 400,000 interments,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DavenportMissingFunds_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-DavenportMissingFunds-1">[1]</a></sup> the cemetery has the second-largest number of burials of any national cemetery in the United States. The largest of the 130 national cemeteries is the <a href="/wiki/Calverton_National_Cemetery" title="Calverton National Cemetery">Calverton National Cemetery</a>, on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_Island,_New_York" title="Long Island, New York">Long Island</a>, near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverhead,_New_York" title="Riverhead, New York">Riverhead, New York</a>, which conducts more than 7,000 burials each year.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1145" data-file-width="1798" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg/300px-6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg/450px-6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg/600px-6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:6707-MilitaryFuneralProcession-ArlingtonlCemetery.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Military_funeral#United_States" title="Military funeral">Military funeral</a> procession in Arlington National Cemetery, July 1967</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to in-ground burial, the cemetery also has one of the larger <a href="/wiki/Columbarium" title="Columbarium">columbaria</a> for cremated remains in the country. Four courts are currently in use, each with 5,000 niches. When construction is complete, there will be nine courts with a total of 50,000 niches; capacity for 100,000 remains. Any honorably discharged veteran is eligible for inurnment in the columbarium, if s/he served on active duty at some point in her/his career (other than for training).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFR_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-CFR-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burial_criteria">Burial criteria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Burial criteria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Part 553 (Army National Military Cemeteries) of <a href="/wiki/Title_32_of_the_Code_of_Federal_Regulations" title="Title 32 of the Code of Federal Regulations">Title 32 of the Code of Federal Regulations</a> (CFR) establishes regulations for the cemetery, including eligibility for interment (ground burial) and inurnment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Due to limited space, the criteria for ground burial eligibility are more restrictive than at other national cemeteries, as well as more restrictive than for inurnment in the columbarium.</p>
<p>The persons specified below are eligible for ground burial in the cemetery, unless otherwise prohibited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The last period of active duty of former members of the armed forces must have ended honorably. Interment may be of casketed or cremated remains.</p>
<ul>
<li>Any active-duty member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">armed forces</a> (except those members serving on active duty for training only).</li>
<li>Any veteran who is retired and eligible for retirement pay from service in the armed forces (including service members retired from a reserve component who served a period of active duty (other than for training)).</li>
<li>Any former member of the armed forces separated honorably prior to October 1, 1949, for medical reasons and who was rated at 30% or greater disabled effective on the day of discharge.</li>
<li>Any former member of the armed forces who has been awarded one of the following decorations:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Cross_(United_States)" title="Distinguished Service Cross (United States)">Distinguished Service Cross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navy_Cross" title="Navy Cross">Navy Cross</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Cross_(United_States)" title="Air Force Cross (United States)">Air Force Cross</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silver_Star" title="Silver Star">Silver Star</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Purple_Heart" title="Purple Heart">Purple Heart</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Any former member of the armed forces who served on active duty (other than for training) and who held any of the following positions:
<ul>
<li>An elective office of the U.S. Government (such as a term in Congress).</li>
<li>Office of the Chief Justice of the United States or of an Associate Justice of the Supreme Court of the United States.</li>
<li>An office listed, at the time the person held the position, in 5 USC 5312 or 5313 (Levels I and II of the Executive Schedule).</li>
<li>The chief of a mission who was at any time during his/her tenure classified in Class I under the provisions of Section 411, Act of August 13, 1946, 60 Stat. 1002, as amended (22 USC 866) or as listed in State Department memorandum dated March 21, 1988.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Any former prisoner of war who, while a prisoner of war, served honorably in the active military, naval, or air service, whose last period of military, naval or air service terminated honorably and who died on or after November 30, 1993.</li>
<li>The spouse, widow or widower, minor child, or permanently dependent child, and certain unmarried adult children of any of the above eligible veterans.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Silence_and_Respect.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1200" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Silence_and_Respect.jpg/150px-Silence_and_Respect.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Silence_and_Respect.jpg/225px-Silence_and_Respect.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Silence_and_Respect.jpg/300px-Silence_and_Respect.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Silence_and_Respect.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Respectful silence is requested at the Arlington National Cemetery.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The widow or widower of:
<ul>
<li>a member of the armed forces who was lost or buried at sea or fell out of a plane or officially determined to be permanently absent with a status of either missing or missing in action.</li>
<li>a member of the armed forces who is interred in a US military cemetery overseas that is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/American_Battle_Monuments_Commission" title="American Battle Monuments Commission">American Battle Monuments Commission</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The spouse, minor child, or permanently dependent child of any person already buried in Arlington National Cemetery.</li>
<li>The parents of a minor child, or permanently dependent child whose remains, based on the eligibility of a parent, are already buried at Arlington. A spouse divorced from the primary eligible, or widowed and remarried, is not eligible for interment.</li>
<li>Provided certain conditions are met, a former member of the armed forces may be buried in the same grave with a close relative who is already buried and is the primary eligible.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inurnment_criteria_for_columbarium">Inurnment criteria for columbarium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Inurnment criteria for columbarium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due at least partly to the lack of space at the cemetery for ground burial, standards for inurnment (burial of cremated remains) in the columbarium are currently much less restrictive than for ground burial at the cemetery. In general, any former member of the armed forces who served on active duty (other than for training) and whose last service terminated honorably is eligible for inurnment. Eligibility for inurnment is described fully in <a class="external text" href="http://ecfr.gpoaccess.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?c=ecfr;sid=ebe6204b5183f9156bf1036a1135dc30;rgn=div5;view=text;node=32%3A3.1.1.4.18;idno=32;cc=ecfr#32:3.1.1.4.18.0.11.16" rel="nofollow">32 C.F.R. § 553.15a</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prohibitions_against_interment_or_memorialization">Prohibitions against interment or memorialization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Prohibitions against interment or memorialization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Congress has from time to time created prohibited categories of persons that, even if otherwise eligible for burial, lose that eligibility. One such prohibition is against certain persons who are convicted of committing certain state or federal capital crimes, as defined in <a class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/38/2411-" rel="nofollow">38 U.S. Code § 2411</a>. Capital crime is a specifically defined term in the statute, and for state offenses can include offenses that are eligible for a life sentence (with or without parole). The reasoning for this provision originally was to prevent <a href="/wiki/Timothy_McVeigh" title="Timothy McVeigh">Timothy McVeigh</a> from being eligible at Arlington National Cemetery, but it has since been amended to prevent others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fox_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-fox-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also prohibited under the same <a class="external text" href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/search/display.html?terms=arlington%20national%20cemetery&amp;url=/uscode/html/uscode38/usc_sec_38_00002411----000-.html%20" rel="nofollow">statute</a> are those determined, with clear and convincing evidence, to have avoided such conviction by death or flight.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_burials">Notable burials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notable burials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_people_buried_at_Arlington_National_Cemetery" title="List of people buried at Arlington National Cemetery">List of people buried at Arlington National Cemetery</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3414" data-file-width="5129" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg/220px-USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg/330px-USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg/440px-USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USA-Arlington_National_Cemetery2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The grave marker of former US President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first soldier to be buried in Arlington was Private <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Christman" title="William Henry Christman">William Henry Christman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> on May 13, 1864.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> There are 396 <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a> recipients buried in Arlington National Cemetery,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> nine of whom are <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a>.</p>
<p>Five <a href="/wiki/State_funeral" title="State funeral">state funerals</a> have been held at Arlington: those of Presidents <a href="/wiki/William_Howard_Taft" title="William Howard Taft">William Howard Taft</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, his two brothers, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Senator" title="United States Senator">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Edward "Ted" Kennedy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/General_of_the_Armies" title="General of the Armies">General of the Armies</a> <a href="/wiki/John_J._Pershing" title="John J. Pershing">John J. Pershing</a>. Whether or not they were wartime service members, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. presidents</a> are eligible to be buried at Arlington, since they oversaw the armed forces as <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commanders-in-chief</a>.</p>
<p>Among the most frequently visited sites in the cemetery is the grave of President <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis</a> who is buried nearby along with their son Patrick and their stillborn daughter Arabella. His remains were interred there on March 14, 1967, a reinterment from his original Arlington burial site, some 20 feet (6.1 m) away, where he was buried in November 1963. The grave is marked with <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Eternal_Flame" title="John F. Kennedy Eternal Flame">an "eternal flame"</a>. The remains of his brothers, Senator <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> and Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Kennedy" title="Ted Kennedy">Edward M. "Ted" Kennedy</a>, are buried nearby. The latter two graves are marked with simple crosses and footstones. On December 1, 1971, <a href="/wiki/Grave_of_Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Grave of Robert F. Kennedy">Robert Kennedy's body was re-interred</a> 100 feet (30 m) from its original June 1968 burial site.</p>
<p>Two of the astronauts who were killed in January 27, 1967 flash fire inside the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_1" title="Apollo 1">Apollo 1</a> Command Module, <a href="/wiki/Gus_Grissom" title="Gus Grissom">Gus Grissom</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roger_Chaffee" title="Roger Chaffee">Roger Chaffee</a>, are buried at the cemetery. <a href="/wiki/John_Glenn" title="John Glenn">John Glenn</a>, the first American to orbit Earth and a longtime U.S. Senator from Ohio, was buried at the cemetery in April 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Diplomat" title="Diplomat">Diplomat</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_Marshal" title="Field Marshal">Field Marshal</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Dill" title="John Dill">John Dill</a> was buried at the cemetery when he died in Washington D.C. during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The equestrian statue on Dill's grave is one of only two such statues at the cemetery; the other is Major General <a href="/wiki/Philip_Kearny" title="Philip Kearny">Philip Kearny</a>'s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Visitor_requirements">Visitor requirements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Visitor requirements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The cemetery has within recent years announced policies and procedures that limit visitor access to the cemetery's grounds. The Cemetery's executive director has stated that some of these may create delays for visitors. Some have become controversial.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle_use_policy">Bicycle use policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Bicycle use policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 6, 2013, Patrick Hallinan, Executive Director, Army National Military Cemeteries, issued an official memorandum that contained the cemetery's then-current bicycle use policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup> The memorandum permitted cyclists to travel in only one direction on only one route unless otherwise authorized by the executive director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup> This "White Line" route traveled from the Old Post Chapel gate at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Myer-Henderson_Hall" title="Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall">Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall</a> towards the main entrance of the cemetery at Memorial Avenue, using Meigs Drive, Sherman Drive and Schley Drive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-2"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup> The memorandum stated without explanation: ″Bicycle traffic will not be permitted to travel in the reverse direction, ....″.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-3"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cyclists could only use this route between 8:00 a.m. and 6:45 p.m. from April 1 to September 30 and between 8:00 a.m. and 4:45 p.m. from October 1 to March 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-4"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup> Cyclists had to wear bicycle helmets that certain designated organizations had approved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-5"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup> Bicycles had to be equipped with headlights, tail lights or red reflectors in lieu of tail lights, regardless of the time of travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memorandum_116-6"><a href="#cite_note-memorandum-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 11, 2016, the Department of the Army published in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Register" title="Federal Register">Federal Register</a> a proposed rule that would, among other things, prohibit a visitor to an Army National Military Cemetery (Arlington National Cemetery and the United States Soldiers' and Airmen's Home National Cemetery) from riding a bicycle without first acquiring a pass to visit a relative's gravesite or columbarium niche.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> After receiving 13 comments from 13 individuals concerning the use of bicycles in the cemetery (including comments from representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia#Government_and_politics" title="Arlington County, Virginia">Arlington County Board</a> and local bicycle advocacy groups that opposed the new restrictions), the Department of the Army published a final rule in the Federal Register on September 26, 2016, that implemented the proposed rule, effective October 26, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>In accordance with the final rule, the cemetery issued a new bicycle use policy, effective October 26, 2016. The policy stated that bicycling would no longer be allowed on Cemetery grounds without a family pass. The policy further stated that "bicyclists traversing the cemetery grounds do impact funeral services and the experience that families expect and deserve as they visit their loved one’s grave. .... As there are no bike paths on the cemetery grounds, mixing cyclists with pedestrians and vehicles creates a safety hazard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_procedures">Security procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Security procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 2016, Hallinan announced that the cemetery was increasing security measures for its visitors. In addition to random identification checks and other security measures already in place, the cemetery will require pedestrians to enter at set access points: the main entrance on Memorial Avenue, the Ord and Weitzel gate, and the Old Post Chapel gate at Joint Base Myer-Henderson Hall. Before entering the cemetery through its main entrance, all pedestrians will be screened through the cemetery's Welcome Center. All vehicle access will require presenting valid, government-issued photo identification, such as a driver’s license or passport, when entering the cemetery. Vehicles will also be subject to random inspections. Hallinan stated that these processes may result in delays when entering the cemetery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arlington_National_Cemetery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Batman_v_Superman:_Dawn_of_Justice" title="Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice">Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</a>, the cemetery appeared as the backdrop for a <a href="/wiki/State_funerals_in_the_United_States" title="State funerals in the United States">state funeral</a> held for <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> However, the physical filming took place in Michigan, using green screen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>

(B) All lands in the Robert E. Lee Memorial Preservation Zone, other than those lands in the Preservation Zone that the Secretary of the Interior determines must be retained because of the historical significance of such lands or for the maintenance of nearby lands or facilities.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Division+B%3A+Military+Construction+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+1997%3A+Title+XXVIII%E2%80%94General+Provisions%3A+Subtitle+C%E2%80%94Land+Conveyances%3A+Section+2821%28a%29.+Transfer+of+lands%2C+Arlington+National+Cemetery%2C+Arlington%2C+Virginia+%28110+Stat.+2791%E2%80%932792%29&amp;rft.date=1996-09-23&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Public+Law+104-201%3A+National+Defense+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+1997&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gpo.gov%2Ffdsys%2Fpkg%2FPLAW-104publ201%2Fpdf%2FPLAW-104publ201.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Williams-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Williams_29-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Williams_29-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Williams, Rudi, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Forces_Press_Service" title="American Forces Press Service">American Forces Press Service</a> (May 27, 2005). <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100301004218/http://www.defense.gov/news/newsarticle.aspx?id=31562" rel="nofollow">"Arlington National Cemetery Gains 70 Acres of Land"</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a>. <li id="cite_note-law2-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-law2_30-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-law2_30-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-law2_30-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-law2_30-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-law2_30-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.gpo.gov/fdsys/pkg/PLAW-107publ107/pdf/PLAW-107publ107.pdf" rel="nofollow">"Division B: Military Construction Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2002: Title XXVIII—General Provisions: Subtitle E—Other Matters: Section 2863(h): Alternate Site for United States Air Force Memorial, Preservation of Open Space on Arlington Ridge Tract, and Related Land Transfer At Arlington National Cemetery, Virginia: Land Transfer, Section 29 (115 Stat. 1332–1333)"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(pdf)</span>. <i>Public Law 107-107: <a href="/wiki/National_Defense_Authorization_Act" title="National Defense Authorization Act">National Defense Authorization Act</a> for Fiscal Year 2002</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Government_Printing_Office" title="United States Government Printing Office">United States Government Printing Office</a>. December 28, 2001<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">March 16,</span> 2013</span>. <q>SEC. 2863. ALTERNATE SITE FOR UNITED STATES AIR FORCE MEMORIAL, PRESERVATION OF OPEN SPACE ON ARLINGTON RIDGE TRACT, AND RELATED LAND TRANSFER AT ARLINGTON NATIONAL CEMETERY, VIRGINIA..... (h) Land Transfer, Section 29.—(1) Transfer required.—Not later than 30 days after the date of the enactment of this Act, the Secretary of the Interior shall transfer, without reimbursement, to the Secretary of the Army administrative jurisdiction over that portion of Section 29 designated as the interment zone and consisting of approximately 12 acres. The Secretary of the Interior shall modify the boundaries of the George Washington Memorial Parkway as may be necessary to reflect the land transfer required by this subsection. (2) Use of transferred land.—The Secretary of the Army shall use the transferred property for the development of in-ground burial sites and columbarium that are designed to meet the contours of Section 29. (3) Management of remainder.—The Secretary of the Interior shall manage that portion of Section 29 not transferred under this subsection in perpetuity to provide a natural setting and visual buffer for Arlington House, the Robert E. Lee Memorial. (4) Repeal of obsolete law.—Section 2821(a) of the Military Construction Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 1997 (division B of Public Law 104-201; 110 Stat. 2791) is repealed.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Division+B%3A+Military+Construction+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2002%3A+Title+XXVIII%E2%80%94General+Provisions%3A+Subtitle+E%E2%80%94Other+Matters%3A+Section+2863%28h%29%3A+Alternate+Site+for+United+States+Air+Force+Memorial%2C+Preservation+of+Open+Space+on+Arlington+Ridge+Tract%2C+and+Related+Land+Transfer+At+Arlington+National+Cemetery%2C+Virginia%3A+Land+Transfer%2C+Section+29+%28115+Stat.+1332%E2%80%931333%29&amp;rft.date=2001-12-28&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Public+Law+107-107%3A+National+Defense+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2002&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.gpo.gov%2Ffdsys%2Fpkg%2FPLAW-107publ107%2Fpdf%2FPLAW-107publ107.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

(a) Land Transfer Required.—The Secretary of Defense shall provide for the transfer to the Secretary of the Army of administrative jurisdiction over three parcels of real property consisting of approximately 36 acres and known as the Navy Annex (in this section referred to as the "Navy Annex property").<br/>
(b) Use of Land.—Subject to paragraph (2), the Secretary of the Army shall incorporate the Navy Annex property transferred under subsection (a) into Arlington National Cemetery.<br/>
(2) ... TRANSFER FROM FORT MYER, ARLINGTON, VIRGINIA.(a) Land Transfer Required.—The Secretary of the Army shall modify the boundaries of Arlington National Cemetery and of Fort Myer to include in Arlington National Cemetery the following parcels of real property situated in Fort Myer, Arlington, Virginia: (1) A parcel comprising approximately five acres bounded by the Fort Myer Post Traditional Chapel to the southwest, McNair Road to the northwest, the Vehicle Maintenance Complex to the northeast, and the masonry wall of Arlington National Cemetery to the southeast. (a) Exchange Authorized.--The Secretary of Defense may convey to Arlington County, Virginia (in this section referred to as the "County"), all right, title, and interest of the United States in and to a parcel of real property, together with any improvements thereon, that consists of not more than 4.5 acres and is located north of Columbia Pike on the Navy Annex property in Arlington County, Virginia, for the purpose of the construction of a freedmen heritage museum and an Arlington history museum. (b) Consideration.—As consideration for the conveyance of the real property under subsection (a), the County shall convey to the United States all right, title, and interest of the County in and to a parcel of real property, together with any improvements thereon, that is of a size equivalent to the total acreage of the real property conveyed by the Secretary under subsection (a) and is located in the area known as the Southgate Road right-of-way between Arlington National Cemetery, Virginia, and the Navy Annex property..... (g) Inclusion of Southgate Road Right-of-Way Property in Transfer of Navy Annex Property for Arlington National Cemetery.—Subsection (a) of section 2881 of the Military Construction Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2000 (division B of Public Law 106-65; 113 Stat. 879) is amended by striking "three parcels of real property consisting of approximately 36 acres" and inserting "four parcels of real property consisting of approximately 40 acres".</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Division+B%3A+Military+Construction+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2005%3A+Title+XXVIII%E2%80%94General+Provisions%3A+Subtitle+D%E2%80%94Land+Conveyances%3A+Part+IV+%E2%80%94+Other+Conveyances%3A+Section+2881.+Land+Exchange%2C+Arlington+County%2C+Virginia+%28118+Stat.+2153%E2%80%932154%29&amp;rft.date=2004-10-28&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Public+Law+108-375%3A+Ronald+W.+Reagan+National+Defense+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2005&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dod.gov%2Fdodgc%2Folc%2Fdocs%2FPL108-375.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-RuaneWarriors-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-RuaneWarriors_35-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-RuaneWarriors_35-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-RuaneWarriors_35-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Ruane, Michael E. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 31,</span> 2012</span>. <q>The Millennium expansion has involved, among other things, the sensitive transfer of 12 acres within the cemetery from the National Park Service's historic Arlington House, the onetime home of Robert E. Lee. The Park Service has lamented the likely loss of woodland and the cemetery's encroachment on the majestic hilltop home, which dates to 1802. The project, which focuses on the northwest edge of the cemetery, includes expansion into about 10 acres taken from the Army's adjacent Fort Myer and four acres of cemetery maintenance property inside the boundaries, officials said. The extra space would provide room for 14,000 ground burials and 22,000 inurnments in a large columbarium complex, officials said. The project comes on the heels of extensive work underway to utilize 40 acres of unused space in the cemetery, creating room for 26,000 more graves and 5,000 inurnments. And there are plans for further outside expansion in the years ahead.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=For+Warriors+Past+and+Future&amp;rft.aufirst=Michael+E.&amp;rft.aulast=Ruane&amp;rft.date=2007-10-07&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.washingtonpost.com%2Fwp-dyn%2Fcontent%2Farticle%2F2007%2F10%2F06%2FAR2007100601090.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Vogel, Steve (August 11, 1998). <a class="external text" href="https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/washingtonpost/doc/408384852.html" rel="nofollow">"Arlington Cemetery Proposal Put on Hold; Officials Say Plan to Transfer Land From Navy Annex, Fort Myer Needs Review"</a>. <i>The Washington Post</i>. p. B3. <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140730013211/http://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/washingtonpost/doc/408384852.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> from the original on 30 July 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 29,</span> 2014</span>. <q>A congressional proposal to expand Arlington National Cemetery onto land now occupied by the Navy Annex and Fort Myer has been at least temporarily put on hold, but officials predicted that in the long term, at least some of the property may be turned into grave sites.<br/>
Members of a House-Senate conference committee said yesterday they have agreed to remove language from a Defense Department appropriations bill that would have transferred the land to the cemetery, which is approaching full capacity.<br/>
(Bob) Stump's proposal, attached to a bill that cleared the House earlier this summer, would have transferred 36.5 acres from the Navy Annex and eight acres from Fort Myer to Arlington Cemetery. The move would create sufficient burial sites to last until 2040, officials said. The proposal has sparked anxiety in Arlington County, where community leaders complained that they had not been consulted about such a major decision.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Arlington+Cemetery+Proposal+Put+on+Hold%3B+Officials+Say+Plan+to+Transfer+Land+From+Navy+Annex%2C+Fort+Myer+Needs+Review&amp;rft.aufirst=Steve&amp;rft.aulast=Vogel&amp;rft.date=1998-08-11&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Washington+Post&amp;rft.pages=B3&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpqasb.pqarchiver.com%2Fwashingtonpost%2Fdoc%2F408384852.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 18,</span> 2017</span>. <q>SEC. 2829A. LAND ACQUISITIONS, ARLINGTON COUNTY, VIRGINIA.(a) ACQUISITION AUTHORIZED.—(1) IN GENERAL.—The Secretary of the Army may acquire by purchase, exchange, donation, or by other means, including condemnation, which the Secretary determines is sufficient for the expansion of Arlington National Cemetery for purposes of ensuring maximization of interment sites and compatible use of adjacent properties, including any appropriate cemetery or memorial parking, all right, title, and interest in and to land—<br/>
(A) from Arlington County (in this section referred to as the ‘‘County’’), one or more parcels of real property in the area known as the Southgate Road right-of-way, Columbia Pike right-of-way, and South Joyce Street right-of-way located in Arlington County, Virginia; and<br/>
(B) from the Commonwealth of Virginia (in this section referred to as the ‘‘Commonwealth’’), one or more parcels of property in the area known as the Columbia Pike right-of-way, including the Washington Boulevard-Columbia Pike interchange, but excluding the Virginia Department of Transportation Maintenance and Operations Facility. ....</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Division+B%3A+Military+Construction+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2017%3A+Title+XXVIII%E2%80%94Military+Construction+General+Provisions%3A+Subtitle+C%E2%80%94Land+Conveyances%3A+Sec.+2829A.+Land+Acquisitions%2C+Arlington+County%2C+Virginia&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Public+Law+114-328%3A+National+Defense+Authorization+Act+for+Fiscal+Year+2017&amp;rft.pages=130+STAT.+2728-130+STAT.+2730&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gpo.gov%2Ffdsys%2Fpkg%2FPLAW-114publ328%2Fpdf%2FPLAW-114publ328.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 17,</span> 2017</span>. <q>(c) ... Specifically, no person shall: .... (8) Ride a bicycle or similar conveyance in an Army National Military Cemetery, except with a proper pass issued by the Executive Director to visit a gravesite or niche. An individual visiting a relative's gravesite or niche may be issued a temporary pass by the Executive Director to proceed directly to and from the gravesite or niche on a bicycle or similar vehicle or conveyance.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=81+FR+29230%3A+Proposed+rule%3A++Amendments+to+32+CFR+553.33+%28Visitors+rules+for+Army+National+Military+Cemeteries%29&amp;rft.au=Department+of+the+Army%2C+Department+of+Defense&amp;rft.date=2016-05-11&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Federal+Register&amp;rft.pages=29230-29243&amp;rft.volume=81&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.federalregister.gov%2Fdocuments%2F2016%2F05%2F11%2F2016-11038%2Farmy-national-military-cemeteries&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 17,</span> 2017</span>. <q>(c) ... Specifically, no person shall: .... (8) Ride a bicycle or similar conveyance in an Army National Military Cemetery, except with a proper pass issued by the Executive Director to visit a gravesite or niche. An individual visiting a relative's gravesite or niche may be issued a temporary pass by the Executive Director to proceed directly to and from the gravesite or niche on a bicycle or similar vehicle or conveyance.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=81+FR+65875%3A+Final+rule%3A++Amendments+to+32+CFR+553.33+%28Visitors+rules+for+Army+National+Military+Cemeteries%29&amp;rft.au=Department+of+the+Army%2C+Department+of+Defense&amp;rft.date=2016-09-26&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Federal+Register&amp;rft.pages=65875-65888&amp;rft.volume=81&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.federalregister.gov%2Fdocuments%2F2016%2F09%2F26%2F2016-23087%2Farmy-national-military-cemeteries&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span><br/>
(2) <cite class="citation news">Wentling, Nikki (October 18, 2016). <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170717205551/https://www.stripes.com/news/arlington-national-cemetery-to-impose-bicycle-ban-1.434693#.WW0kjdyQy70" rel="nofollow">"Arlington National Cemetery to impose bicycle ban"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Stars_and_Stripes_(newspaper)" title="Stars and Stripes (newspaper)">Stars and Stripes</a></i>. Archived from <a class="external text" href="https://www.stripes.com/news/arlington-national-cemetery-to-impose-bicycle-ban-1.434693" rel="nofollow">the original</a> on July 17, 2017. <q>Bicyclists will no longer be allowed to ride through the grounds of Arlington National Cemetery under a new policy that’s set to start next week despite protest from local officials and bicycle groups. Bicyclists disrupt funeral services, affect other visitors’ experiences and pose safety concerns, the Army said in an announcement of the new rule, which goes into effect Oct. 26. But the Arlington County Board and bicycle advocacy organizations in Arlington and nearby Fairfax County argued cyclists using the cemetery do so respectfully.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AArlington+National+Cemetery&amp;rft.atitle=Arlington+National+Cemetery+to+impose+bicycle+ban&amp;rft.aufirst=Nikki&amp;rft.aulast=Wentling&amp;rft.date=2016-10-18&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Stars+and+Stripes&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.stripes.com%2Fnews%2Farlington-national-cemetery-to-impose-bicycle-ban-1.434693&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
